<div id="review_562536765" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/562536765" />
    <a title="Allie Riley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17643421-allie-riley"><img alt="Allie Riley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522840920p2/17643421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/562536765?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allie Riley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allie Riley" href="/user/show/17643421-allie-riley">Allie Riley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099284796" href="/book/show/895680.The_Sailor_Who_Fell_from_Grace_with_the_Sea">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer562536765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15482725819034826355">I didn't quite finish it, actually, I got to page 165. But I was so revolted by what was evidently going to happen next that I refused to read further.<br/><br/>Fusako Kuroda, a successful business woman, has been a widow for 5 years. By chance when visiting his ship with her 13 year-old son Noboru, she meets Ryuji Tsukazaki the Second Mate. She invites him to dinner, one thing leads to another (as it does), they fall in love and he decides to abandon his life on the sea in order to marry her. So far so n</span>
  <span id="freeText15482725819034826355" style="display:none">I didn't quite finish it, actually, I got to page 165. But I was so revolted by what was evidently going to happen next that I refused to read further.<br /><br />Fusako Kuroda, a successful business woman, has been a widow for 5 years. By chance when visiting his ship with her 13 year-old son Noboru, she meets Ryuji Tsukazaki the Second Mate. She invites him to dinner, one thing leads to another (as it does), they fall in love and he decides to abandon his life on the sea in order to marry her. So far so normal. Meanwhile, her son is a member of a violent and unpleasant gang. There are six of them: Chief and numbers one through to five. Noboru is number three. The gang is united by a very bizarre and depressing philosophy. They appear to believe that only death is worth while and that therefore the act of procreation is to be despised. Thus by extension all fathers are evil. Since Ryuji has renounced his former maritime life and taken on the role of father, they decide that he must be punished. I abandoned the book at the point at which they begin to delineate the method of punishment.<br /><br />So, one star is awarded for the sublimely beautiful prose. There is no denying that this man could write. It is achingly gorgeous. The other star is for the well-rounded characters of Ryuji and Fusako and their sweet romance. However, further than that I will not go. The life philosophy he evidently espoused was bleak and depressing. And I refuse point blank to forgive him for the kitten killing scene which was brutal, sickening and wholly unnecessary. Unless you have a particularly strong stomach or are of a particularly cynical frame of mind I would avoid this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15482725819034826355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2535635285" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2535635285" />
    <a title="WhatIReallyRead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52500467-whatireallyread"><img alt="WhatIReallyRead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483674713p2/52500467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2535635285?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="WhatIReallyRead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="WhatIReallyRead" href="/user/show/52500467-whatireallyread">WhatIReallyRead</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=translated">translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=great-writing">great-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=creepy">creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52500467-whatireallyread?shelf=japanese">japanese</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2535635285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7686215822466180971"><b>What a weird book.</b><br/><br/>The Sailor Who Fell from Grace with the Sea was perplexing, confusing, immersive, compelling, creepy, heart-warming, sometimes icky, sometimes downright scary. It contained cruelty, graphic violence, and a very romantic love story. It kept me wondering: "Where is this going? Is there a point to this?" <br/><br/>I haven't read any of Mishima's other books, and very few books by Japanese authors in general. But the impressions inspired by The Sailor Who Fell from Grace rang surprisingly fa</span>
  <span id="freeText7686215822466180971" style="display:none"><b>What a weird book.</b><br /><br />The Sailor Who Fell from Grace with the Sea was perplexing, confusing, immersive, compelling, creepy, heart-warming, sometimes icky, sometimes downright scary. It contained cruelty, graphic violence, and a very romantic love story. It kept me wondering: "Where is this going? Is there a point to this?" <br /><br />I haven't read any of Mishima's other books, and very few books by Japanese authors in general. But the impressions inspired by The Sailor Who Fell from Grace rang surprisingly familiar, reminding me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17803.After_Dark" title="After Dark by Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">After Dark</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3354.Haruki_Murakami" title="Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Haruki Murakami</a>. <br /><br />I was captivated by this book. The atmosphere of a sea-port and the life in it was conveyed well. What I liked most about this book was the writing and characters. People inhabiting The Sailor Who Fell from Grace were alive, vibrant, real. The <b>ending was very powerful</b>. And terrible. I think I screamed for an hour straight. <br /><br />I felt like there was a symbolic meaning to this book as well, though I may not be educated enough to fully grasp it. I want to read more books by Japanese authors, and I'll certainly pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62805.The_Sound_of_Waves" title="The Sound of Waves by Yukio Mishima" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sound of Waves</a>.<br /><br />I've just read a brief bio of Mishima on Wiki - and WOW. This dude is hardcore. No wonder his book is as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7686215822466180971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2352646795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2352646795" />
    <a title="Sohaib" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31777090-sohaib"><img alt="Sohaib" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599511226p2/31777090.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2352646795?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sohaib" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sohaib" href="/user/show/31777090-sohaib">Sohaib</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31777090-sohaib?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2352646795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3308602461762559082"><b>Four stars and a half.</b><br/><br/>I love patterns in literature—motifs that keep coming up from time immemorial. In this book, it's the boy who unconsciously wants to save mommy from daddy. Oedipus was guilty of that, hence, the Oedipus complex, the boy infinitely tied to the mother. <br/><br/><blockquote>"He could no longer distinguish cause from effect; possibly this unreasonable yearning for his mother was due to a desire to wound her even if he had to share the pain."</blockquote><br/><br/><i>
  <u>
    <b>The Story</b>
  </u>
</i><br/><br/>Fusako Kuroda, 33, is a single mother</span>
  <span id="freeText3308602461762559082" style="display:none"><b>Four stars and a half.</b><br /><br />I love patterns in literature—motifs that keep coming up from time immemorial. In this book, it's the boy who unconsciously wants to save mommy from daddy. Oedipus was guilty of that, hence, the Oedipus complex, the boy infinitely tied to the mother. <br /><br /><blockquote>"He could no longer distinguish cause from effect; possibly this unreasonable yearning for his mother was due to a desire to wound her even if he had to share the pain."</blockquote><br /><br /><i>
  <u>
    <b>The Story</b>
  </u>
</i><br /><br />Fusako Kuroda, 33, is a single mother, a proprietress of a fine luxury shop. Noboru, 13, is her only son—obsessed with peeping at her from a peephole in the wall their separate bedrooms share. Things get better when his mother meets a sailor called Ryuji and invites him over. Better were it not for Kuroda's most influential acquaintance, the Chief, the leader of his secret brotherhood, the one who instills his neurosis (Father hatred; the Father in his many forms) in the hearts and minds of his friends. <br /><br />Recommended.</span>

<div id="review_2195462885" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2195462885" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099284796" href="/book/show/895680.The_Sailor_Who_Fell_from_Grace_with_the_Sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2195462885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10158719713791601741">Oooh that blasted father figure! <br/><br/>Either he is doing my mom or he is not doing it well enough - anyway I hate him because he does not comply with my new-found 13-year old nihilistic world view. <br/><br/>I have no previous experiences with the late Mr. Mishima and I´m seriously afraid this is going to be the only one.<br/>The symbolism is to fat for my taste the Japanese equivalent to Coelho …<br/><br/>3 stars for being well written though. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1576611072" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1576611072" />
    <a title="Brown Girl Reading" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2682140-brown-girl-reading"><img alt="Brown Girl Reading" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460474568p2/2682140.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1576611072?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brown Girl Reading" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brown Girl Reading" href="/user/show/2682140-brown-girl-reading">Brown Girl Reading</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099492696" href="/book/show/578364.The_Sailor_who_Fell_from_Grace_with_the_Sea">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Japanese Lit</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Brown Girl Reading by: </span>
      Conrad
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1576611072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11163265098680544431">I gave this one 2,5 stars. It was heavy on symbolism and extreme and utopian in it ideals on glory and honour. I didn't love it but it's certainly unforgettable in plot. The thing it really has going for it is Mishima's writing, which is precise, calculating, and incisive. I would suggest starting with Patriotism for new readers of Mishima.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2264279324" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2264279324" />
    <a title="Zak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68295640-zak"><img alt="Zak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500708503p2/68295640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2264279324?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zak" href="/user/show/68295640-zak">Zak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68295640-zak?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2264279324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7744994156041034664">Captivating writing although I had minor problems with the content. A widow takes her teenage son on a ship visit (he is crazy about ships). She hits it off with the 2nd Officer and they are soon an item. The son is part of a nerdy gang from school. Initially he is in awe of the officer but soon things take a dark turn. <br/><br/>So what about the content didn't I like? Firstly, the group of 13-year old teenagers is rather annoying. There is a lot of facile talk about life, fathers, etc., filled with sill</span>
  <span id="freeText7744994156041034664" style="display:none">Captivating writing although I had minor problems with the content. A widow takes her teenage son on a ship visit (he is crazy about ships). She hits it off with the 2nd Officer and they are soon an item. The son is part of a nerdy gang from school. Initially he is in awe of the officer but soon things take a dark turn. <br /><br />So what about the content didn't I like? Firstly, the group of 13-year old teenagers is rather annoying. There is a lot of facile talk about life, fathers, etc., filled with silly concepts which got tiresome. Secondly, the man in the story (the 2nd Officer) kept fantasising about seeking out his 'Great Cause' and dying a glorious death. I gather the author allowed his own world views to seep into the character. Perhaps a longing for Japan's return to its former glory after the loss of WWII. All in all, not a very enlightened view. Still, a worthwhile read just for the writing.<br /><br />Final rating: 3.75*</span>
  <a data-text-id="7744994156041034664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3175779338" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1991298-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528559847p2/1991298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3175779338?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana" href="/user/show/1991298-ana">Ana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781784875428" href="/book/show/43459809-the-sailor-who-fell-from-grace-with-the-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1991298-ana?shelf=modern-classics">modern-classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1991298-ana?shelf=own-and-read">own-and-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1991298-ana?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3175779338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17024610538689626487">Poetic, yet unbearably misogynistic. <br/><br/>Mishima just couldn’t help himself, could he? Everything has to be an ode to “the brute power of his own manhood,” while women are just body parts, lamenting the absence of men. Ugh! And don’t tell me that such was the nature of those times, when the author goes out of his way to find new metaphors to describe said manhood. I’m having <i>Spring Snow</i> flashbacks!<br/><br/>I can’t help but imagine him and Freud having an afternoon tea, bonding over father figures and phallic</span>
  <span id="freeText17024610538689626487" style="display:none">Poetic, yet unbearably misogynistic. <br /><br />Mishima just couldn’t help himself, could he? Everything has to be an ode to “the brute power of his own manhood,” while women are just body parts, lamenting the absence of men. Ugh! And don’t tell me that such was the nature of those times, when the author goes out of his way to find new metaphors to describe said manhood. I’m having <i>Spring Snow</i> flashbacks!<br /><br />I can’t help but imagine him and Freud having an afternoon tea, bonding over father figures and phallic narcissism.</span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2009456481?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/17629329-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/30371004-the-sailor-who-fell-from-grace-with-the-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17629329-leah?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17629329-leah?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17629329-leah?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2009456481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6135811536578830281">A nasty little book about nasty little boys being nasty. I tolerated the boy spying on his naked mother's body and later on her having sex. I put up with the pretentious, unrealistic conversations the boys have about the existential emptiness of life. But I abandoned it when they were getting ready to kill a kitten for fun. Not for me. But literary critics love it, of course.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('o0I+bhhAobwU2cWVmEL/QtbP/t7sC05tmG4x3ENBErc8x3CraOyOui0g9nyUx7lXGmqJT0Xi43DfNtwSy3h2Ug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Osamu Dazai’s The Setting Sun takes this milieu as its background to<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5180530598616916959\" style=\"display:none\">The post-war period in Japan was one of immense social change as Japanese society adjusted to the shock of defeat and to the occupation of Japan by American forces and their allies. Osamu Dazai’s The Setting Sun takes this milieu as its background to tell the story of the decline of a minor aristocratic family.\n\nThe story is told through the eyes of Kazuko, the unmarried daughter of a widowed aristocrat. Her search for self meaning in a society devoid of use for her forms the crux of Dazai’s novel. It is a sad story, and structurally is a novel very much within the confines of the Japanese take on the novel in a way reminiscent of authors such as Nobel Prize winner Yasunari Kawabata – the social interactions are peripheral and understated, nuances must be drawn, and for readers more used to Western novelistic forms this comes across as being rather wishy-washy.\n\nKazuko’s mother falls ill, and due to their financial circumstances they are forced to take a cottage in the countryside. Her brother, who became addicted to opium during the war is missing. When he returns, Kazuko attempts to form a liaison with the novelist Uehara. This romantic displacement only furthers to deepen her alienation from society.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5180530598616916959\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return Mikage, the heroine of Kitchen, is an orphan raised by her grandmother, who has passed away. Grieving, she is taken in by her friend Yoichi and his mother (who was once his father), Eriko. As the three of them form an improvised family that soon weathers its own tragic losses, Yoshimoto spins a lovely, evocative tale that recalls early Marguerite Duras. Kitchen and its companion story, &quot;Moonlight Shadow,&quot; are elegant tales whose seeming simplicity is the ruse of a writer whose voice echoes in the mind and the soul.<\/span>\n  <a       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/35258.Yukio_Mishima">About Yukio Mishima</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/35258.Yukio_Mishima"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1502325778p3/35258.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8351255867547756933">Yukio Mishima (三島 由紀夫) was born in Tokyo in 1925. He graduated from Tokyo Imperial University’s School of Jurisprudence in 1947. His first published book, <i>The Forest in Full Bloom</i>, appeared in 1944 and he established himself as a major author with <i>Confessions of a Mask</i> (1949). From then until his death he continued to publish novels, short stories, and plays each year. His crowning achievement, th</span>
  <span id="freeText8351255867547756933" style="display:none">Yukio Mishima (三島 由紀夫) was born in Tokyo in 1925. He graduated from Tokyo Imperial University’s School of Jurisprudence in 1947. His first published book, <i>The Forest in Full Bloom</i>, appeared in 1944 and he established himself as a major author with <i>Confessions of a Mask</i> (1949). From then until his death he continued to publish novels, short stories, and plays each year. His crowning achievement, the Sea of Fertility tetralogy—which contains the novels <i>Spring Snow</i> (1969), <i>Runaway Horses</i> (1969), <i>The Temple of Dawn</i> (1970), and <i>The Decay of the Angel</i> (1971)—is considered one of the definitive works of twentieth-century Japanese fiction. In 1970, at the age of forty-five and the day after completing the last novel in the Fertility series, Mishima committed seppuku (ritual suicide)—a spectacular death that attracted worldwide attention.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8351255867547756933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
